Commit the returned pins after attaching the\n// Collection's programs to the required hooks using [commitMapPins].\n//\n// This has two main purposes: replacing pins of incompatible maps that are\n// upgraded or downgraded by a different version of the agent, as well as\n// replacing pins of maps that should never be reused/repopulated by the loader,\n// like tail call maps.\n//\n// Letting the loader repopulate an existing tail call map will transition the\n// program through invalid states. For example, code can be moved from one tail\n// call to another, making some instructions execute twice or not at all\n// depending on the order the tail calls were inserted.\nfunc mapsToReplace(toReplace []string, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, coll *ebpf.Collection, opts ebpf.CollectionOptions) ([]toPin, error) {\n\tif opts.Maps.PinPath == \"\" && len(toReplace) > 0 {\n\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"empty Maps.PinPath in CollectionOptions\")\n\t}\n\n\t// We need both Map and MapSpec as the pin path is derived from MapSpec.Name,\n\t// and can be modified before creating the Collection. This is to be called after the Collection's programs have\n// been attached to the required hooks. Any existing pins are overwritten.\nfunc commitMapPins(logger *slog.Logger, pins []toPin) error {\n\tfor _, pin := range pins {\n\t\tif err := os.Remove(pin.path); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, os.ErrNotExist) {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"removing map pin at %s: %w\", pin.path, err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := pin.m.Pin(pin.path); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"pinning map to %s: %w\", pin.path, err)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tlogger.Debug(\"Replaced map pin\", logfields.Pin, pin.path)\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n","numLines":143,"startLine":1,"totalLines":143}}}

Checking whether BPFFS filesystem is mounted in /sys/fs/bpf.\n//  2. If there is no mount, then mount BPFFS in /sys/fs/bpf and finish there.\n//  3. If there is a BPFFS mount, finish there.\n//  4. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01V5Phtd5rt1ysQ7JxL1gVRZ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01UTuHQ7r1cS3rF4bTNocqvf","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Cilium eBPF map API provides comprehensive Go wrappers for user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. This document serves as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.\n\nThe API is organized around the `Map` type, which wraps the underlying kernel map and provides high-level operations like CRUD, iteration, pinning, event subscription, and error recovery.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Map Types and Interfaces](#core-map-types-and-interfaces)\n2. [Map Creation and Lifecycle](#map-creation-and-lifecycle)\n3. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n4. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n5. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n6. [BPF Filesystem Paths](#bpf-filesystem-paths)\n7. [Event System](#event-system)\n8. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n9. [Advanced Features](#advanced-features)\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Types and Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New returns a pointer to a new instance of this MapKey.\n    // Used to allocate memory for iteration and lookups.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Defines the key type for a BPF map. All keys must implement `fmt.Stringer` for logging and string representation.\n\n**Example Implementation**:\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    ID uint32\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &MyKey{}\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyKey{ID: %d}\", k.ID)\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New returns a pointer to a new instance of this MapValue.\n    // Used to allocate memory for iteration and lookups.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Defines the value type for a BPF map. All values must implement `fmt.Stringer`.\n\n**Example Implementation**:\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Counter uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyValue{Counter: %d}\", v.Counter)\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n    // NewSlice returns a pointer to a slice of structs implementing MapValue.\n    // This is used for per-CPU map operations to fetch values from all CPUs.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Extends `MapValue` for per-CPU maps where values are replicated per CPU.\n\n**Example Implementation**:\n```go\ntype PerCPUValue struct {\n    Data uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &PerCPUValue{}\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUValue) NewSlice() any {\n    return make([]PerCPUValue, 0)\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"PerCPUValue{Data: %d}\", v.Data)\n}\n```\n\n### DesiredAction Type\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync\n    Insert                       // Entry needs to be created or updated\n    Delete                       // Entry needs to be deleted\n)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Indicates the synchronization state of a cache entry when map caching is enabled.\n\n### Map Struct\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... unexported fields\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Represents a BPF map in user-space. Provides methods for CRUD operations, iteration, pinning, and event handling.\n\n**Thread-Safety**: The Map type is thread-safe. All operations acquire internal locks (`RWMutex`) as needed.\n\n---\n\n## Map Creation and Lifecycle\n\n### NewMap\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Creates a new Map instance configured for the specified map type and capacities.\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `name`: A base name for the map (will be used as the map name in the kernel and for pinning)\n- `mapType`: The eBPF map type (Hash, LRUHash, Array, etc.)\n- `mapKey`: Template instance for keys (used to determine key size via reflection)\n- `mapValue`: Template instance for values (used to determine value size via reflection)\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: BPF map flags (e.g., BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC)\n\n**Returns**: A new Map instance in an unopened state.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_test_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &TestKey{},\n    &TestValue{},\n    10000,\n    0)\n```\n\n**Note**: The map is not yet opened or created in the kernel. Call `OpenOrCreate()` or `Create()` to materialize it.\n\n### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Creates a new Map with an inner map specification (used for maps of maps).\n\n**Parameters**: Same as `NewMap`, plus:\n- `innerSpec`: The specification for the inner map (for map-of-maps types)\n\n### OpenMap\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Opens an existing map from the BPF filesystem at the absolute pin path.\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map (must be absolute, checked with `path.IsAbs()`)\n- `key`: Template instance for the key type\n- `value`: Template instance for the value type\n\n**Returns**: An opened Map ready for operations, or an error if the map doesn't exist or is incompatible.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm, err := OpenMap(\"/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/my_map\", &TestKey{}, &TestValue{})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n**Note**: The map is immediately opened and ready for use. No additional `Open()` call is needed.\n\n### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Opens an existing pinned map, or creates a new one if it doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- If a pinned map already exists at the map's pin path, attempts to open it\n- If the existing map's attributes (type, key/value sizes, max entries, flags) match the current Map's spec, reuses it\n- If the existing map is incompatible, deletes it and creates a new one\n- If the map is marked as non-persistent, always recreates it\n- The map is pinned to the BPF filesystem by default (with `ebpf.PinByName`)\n\n**Returns**: An error if the operation fails, or nil on success.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// Map is now open and ready for use\n```\n\n### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Creates the map in the kernel without pinning it to the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Creates a new map according to the Map's specification\n- The map is NOT pinned, so it will be destroyed when the file descriptor is closed\n- Useful for temporary maps or when pinning is not desired\n\n**Returns**: An error if creation fails, or nil on success.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"temp_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0)\nif err := m.CreateUnpinned(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Creates the map and immediately closes the file descriptor.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Calls `OpenOrCreate()` to create or open the map\n- Immediately calls `Close()` to release the file descriptor\n- The map remains pinned and accessible through `Open()` later\n- Useful when you only need to ensure the map exists but don't need an open handle\n\n**Returns**: An error if creation or closing fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"persistent_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0)\nif err := m.Create(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Map is pinned and closed. Open it later:\nm2, err := OpenMap(m.Path(), &MyKey{}, &MyValue{})\n```\n\n### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Removes any existing pin and recreates the map from scratch.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Deletes the existing pinned map at the pin path\n- Creates a new map with the current specification\n- Re-pins the new map to the same location\n\n**Returns**: An error if the map is already open, if pin removal fails, or if recreation fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\n// To reset a map to a clean state:\nif err := m.Recreate(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Opens an already-pinned map (does not create it).\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Attempts to load the pinned map from the pin path\n- The map path is determined either from the Map's configured path or by calling `setPathIfUnset()`\n- If the map is already open, this is a no-op\n- Uses read-write locking to serialize access\n\n**Returns**: An error if the pinned map doesn't exist or can't be loaded.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0)\n// Set the path or map name before calling Open()\nif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Closes the map and releases the file descriptor.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- If error synchronization is enabled, removes the associated error resolver controller\n- Closes the underlying kernel map if it's open\n- Deregisters the map from internal tracking\n- If the map is already closed, this is a no-op\n\n**Returns**: Always nil.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n### IsOpen\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns whether the map is currently open.\n\n**Returns**: True if the map has an open file descriptor, false otherwise.\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Looks up a value in the map by key.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a read lock for thread-safe access\n- Returns the value for the given key, or an error if the key is not found\n- The returned value is a new instance allocated by calling `MapValue.New()`\n\n**Returns**: The MapValue for the key, or an error (including `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if not found).\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nvalue, err := m.Lookup(&MyKey{ID: 123})\nif err == ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist {\n    return nil // Key not found\n}\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\nfmt.Println(value.String())\n```\n\n### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Creates or updates a map entry.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a write lock for thread-safe access\n- Updates the map entry with `ebpf.UpdateAny` semantics (insert or overwrite)\n- If caching is enabled, updates the cache entry and marks it as `OK` (in sync)\n- If the update fails and caching is enabled, marks the entry as `Insert` (pending sync) and schedules the error resolver\n- Adds a `MapUpdate` event to the event buffer if enabled\n\n**Returns**: An error if the update fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nerr := m.Update(&MyKey{ID: 123}, &MyValue{Counter: 456})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Deletes a map entry by key.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a write lock\n- Deletes the entry from the map\n- If the key doesn't exist, returns an error (does NOT silently succeed)\n- If caching is enabled, removes the cache entry\n- Adds a `MapDelete` event to the event buffer if enabled\n\n**Returns**: An error if the deletion fails or the key doesn't exist.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nerr := m.Delete(&MyKey{ID: 123})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Deletes a map entry, but returns success if the key doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Same as `Delete()`, but treats `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` as success (returns `false, nil`)\n- Useful when the key might not exist and you don't want to treat that as an error\n\n**Returns**: `(true, nil)` if the entry was deleted, `(false, nil)` if it didn't exist, or `(false, error)` if a real error occurred.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\ndeleted, err := m.SilentDelete(&MyKey{ID: 123})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\nif deleted {\n    fmt.Println(\"Entry was deleted\")\n}\n```\n\n### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Deletes a map entry when the map lock is already held.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Same as `Delete()`, but assumes the caller already holds `m.lock` for writing\n- **MUST be called only from within a `DumpCallback`** or similar context where the lock is already acquired\n- Prevents deadlock when deletion is needed during iteration\n\n**Returns**: An error if the deletion fails.\n\n**Important**: Using `DeleteLocked` outside of a callback where the lock is held will cause data races or deadlocks.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Need to delete entries while iterating?\n    if shouldDelete(key) {\n        // MUST use DeleteLocked here, not Delete\n        err := m.DeleteLocked(key)\n        if err != nil {\n            // Handle error\n        }\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Deletes all entries from a map.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a write lock\n- Iterates over all entries and deletes them individually\n- Updates cache entries as they are deleted\n- Adds a `MapDeleteAll` event to the event buffer\n- Note: If entries are added concurrently during deletion, they may not be deleted\n\n**Returns**: An error if iteration or deletion fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nif err := m.DeleteAll(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Clears all entries from a map by resetting their values to zero.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Only works when events buffer and value cache are disabled\n- Iterates over all entries and updates each with a zero-initialized value\n- Maintains the keys but resets values\n\n**Returns**: An error if events buffer or value cache are enabled, or if the operation fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nif err := m.ClearAll(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Iterates over all entries in a map, calling the callback for each entry.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a read lock for thread-safe iteration\n- For each entry, allocates a new key and value using `MapKey.New()` and `MapValue.New()`\n- Calls the callback with the new key and value instances\n- Callback values are fresh instances and safe to retain\n\n**Returns**: An error if iteration fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"%s -> %s\\n\", key.String(), value.String())\n})\n```\n\n### DumpPerCPUWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Iterates over all entries in a per-CPU map, passing all per-CPU values for each key.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Only works for per-CPU map types (PerCPUHash, PerCPUArray, LRUCPUHash, PerCPUCGroupStorage)\n- The value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n- For each entry, the callback receives a slice of values (one per CPU)\n- Slices are fresh instances and safe to retain\n\n**Returns**: An error if the map is not a per-CPU type, the value doesn't implement `MapPerCPUValue`, or iteration fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nerr := m.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    vals := values.([]PerCPUValue)\n    for cpu, val := range vals {\n        fmt.Printf(\"CPU %d: %s\\n\", cpu, val.String())\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### DumpWithCallbackIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Like `DumpWithCallback`, but returns early if the map doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Checks if the pinned map file exists\n- If it doesn't exist, returns nil (no error)\n- If it exists, calls `DumpWithCallback`\n\n**Returns**: nil if the map doesn't exist, or the result of `DumpWithCallback` if it does.\n\n### DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Iterates over a map while handling concurrent modifications (entries added/deleted during iteration).\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Tracks the previous key and current key to detect and recover from deletion\n- If the current key is deleted during iteration, falls back to the previous key or restarts from the first key\n- Limits iteration to 4× the map's max size to prevent infinite loops if the map is continuously updated\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if this limit is exceeded\n- Populates `DumpStats` with metrics about the iteration process\n- The callback can call `DeleteLocked()` without deadlock concerns\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `cb`: Callback function invoked for each entry\n- `stats`: A `DumpStats` instance (created via `NewDumpStats(m)`) that tracks iteration metrics\n\n**Returns**: `ErrMaxLookup` if the iteration limit is exceeded, or another error if something fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    fmt.Println(key.String(), \"->\", value.String())\n}, stats)\n\nfmt.Printf(\"Lookups: %d, Failed: %d, Interrupted: %d, Completed: %v\\n\",\n    stats.Lookup, stats.LookupFailed, stats.Interrupted, stats.Completed)\n```\n\n### Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Dumps all map entries into a map structure.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Calls `DumpWithCallback` internally\n- For each key-value pair, appends the value string to `hash[key.String()]`\n- The result is a `map[string][]string` where each key may have multiple values\n\n**Returns**: An error if iteration fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nhash := make(map[string][]string)\nif err := m.Dump(hash); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\nfor keyStr, values := range hash {\n    fmt.Printf(\"%s: %v\\n\", keyStr, values)\n}\n```\n\n### DumpIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Like `Dump`, but returns early if the map file doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Checks if the pinned map file exists\n- If it exists, calls `Dump`\n\n**Returns**: nil if the map doesn't exist, or the result of `Dump` if it does.\n\n### BatchIterator\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct { /* ... */ }\n\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Provides a typed wrapper for efficient batched iteration of BPF maps.\n\n**Type Parameters**:\n- `KT`: The key type (must be a struct)\n- `VT`: The value type (must be a struct)\n- `KP`: Key pointer constraint (must be `*KT` and implement `MapKey`)\n- `VP`: Value pointer constraint (must be `*VT` and implement `MapValue`)\n\n**Example**:\n```go\ntype TestKey struct {\n    ID uint32\n}\n\nfunc (k *TestKey) New() MapKey { return &TestKey{} }\nfunc (k *TestKey) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", k.ID) }\n\ntype TestValue struct {\n    Count uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *TestValue) New() MapValue { return &TestValue{} }\nfunc (v *TestValue) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"%d\", v.Count) }\n\n// Create iterator\niter := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n\n// Use with IterateAll\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    fmt.Println(k.ID, \"->\", v.Count)\n}\n\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### BatchIterator.IterateAll\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns an iterator sequence that yields all key-value pairs using the batched API.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Only supports Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie map types\n- Automatically handles batch sizing and retries\n- If a batch lookup fails with `ENOSPC` (no space in buffer), automatically doubles the buffer size and retries (up to a configurable number of times, default 3)\n- Uses an initial buffer size calculated based on the map's max entries\n- Stops and records error on any other error type\n- Returns a `Seq2[KP, VP]` compatible with range loops (Go 1.22+)\n\n**Context**: The iteration respects context cancellation. If the context is cancelled, iteration stops and the error is recorded in `Err()`.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nctx := context.Background()\nfor key, value := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"%d -> %d\\n\", key.ID, value.Count)\n}\n\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### BatchIterator.IterateAll Options\n\n**WithMaxRetries**:\n```go\nfunc WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nSets the maximum number of retries when `ENOSPC` errors occur. Default is 3.\n\n**WithStartingChunkSize**:\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the calculated starting chunk size. Useful when you know the expected hash bucket size.\n\n**WithEBPFBatchOpts**:\n```go\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nPasses custom `ebpf.BatchOptions` to the underlying batch lookup.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx,\n    WithMaxRetries[TestKey, TestValue](5),\n    WithStartingChunkSize[TestKey, TestValue](256),\n) {\n    // Iterate\n}\n```\n\n### BatchIterator.Err\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns any error encountered during iteration.\n\n**Returns**: The error that stopped the iteration, or nil if iteration completed successfully.\n\n### DumpStats\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started          time.Time\n    Finished         time.Time\n    Lookup           uint32  // Number of key lookups\n    LookupFailed     uint32  // Number of failed lookups\n    PrevKeyUnavailable uint32  // Times previous key was unavailable\n    KeyFallback      uint32  // Times iterator fell back to previous key\n    MaxEntries       uint32  // Max entries in the map\n    Interrupted      uint32  // Times iteration was interrupted\n    Completed        bool    // True if iteration completed fully\n}\n\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Tracks statistics for reliable map iteration.\n\n**Duration Method**:\n```go\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\nReturns the elapsed time between start and finish.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Unpin\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Removes the pinned map from the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Determines the pin path from `m.Path()`\n- Calls `os.RemoveAll()` to delete the pinned file or directory\n\n**Returns**: An error if removal fails.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nif err := m.Unpin(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### UnpinIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Removes the pinned map, but returns success if it doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Checks if the map file exists\n- If it doesn't exist, returns nil\n- If it exists, calls `Unpin()`\n\n**Returns**: An error only if the file exists but removal fails.\n\n### Path\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the absolute path to the pinned map on the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- If the path is already set, returns it\n- Otherwise, calls `setPathIfUnset()` which constructs the path from the map name\n\n**Returns**: The absolute path, or an error if the path cannot be determined.\n\n### Name\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the basename of the map (the name used in the kernel).\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nname := m.Name()  // e.g., \"my_map\"\n```\n\n### FD\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the file descriptor of the open map.\n\n**Returns**: The file descriptor, or an invalid value if the map is not open.\n\n---\n\n## BPF Filesystem Paths\n\nThe following functions manage paths in the BPF filesystem:\n\n### BPFFSRoot\n\n```go\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the root directory of the mounted BPF filesystem.\n\n**Default**: `/sys/fs/bpf` (can be overridden with `setBPFFSRoot`)\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nroot := BPFFSRoot()  // e.g., \"/sys/fs/bpf\"\n```\n\n### CiliumPath\n\n```go\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the BPF filesystem path reserved for Cilium objects.\n\n**Returns**: `<BPFFSRoot>/cilium`\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nciliumPath := CiliumPath()  // e.g., \"/sys/fs/bpf/cilium\"\n```\n\n### MapPath\n\n```go\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the absolute path where a BPF map with the given name is (or should be) pinned.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- For Cilium agent: returns `<TCGlobalsPath>/<name>`\n- For other components: queries mount info to find the BPF filesystem path\n\n**Example**:\n```go\npath := MapPath(logger, \"my_map\")  // e.g., \"/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/my_map\"\n```\n\n### TCGlobalsPath\n\n```go\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the path to the legacy TC globals directory.\n\n**Returns**: `<BPFFSRoot>/tc/globals`\n\n### LocalMapName\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Creates a localized name for a map that is specific to an ID.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nlocalName := LocalMapName(\"endpoint\", 42)  // \"endpoint00042\"\n```\n\n### LocalMapPath\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the path for a localized map.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\npath := LocalMapPath(logger, \"endpoint\", 42)  // \"/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/endpoint00042\"\n```\n\n### CheckOrMountFS\n\n```go\nfunc CheckOrMountFS(logger *slog.Logger, bpfRoot string)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Checks or mounts the BPF filesystem and initializes it for use.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Verifies the BPF filesystem is mounted at the specified path (or default locations)\n- If not mounted, attempts to mount it\n- Handles fallback to alternate paths if necessary\n- Fatal error if mounting fails\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `logger`: Logger for diagnostic messages\n- `bpfRoot`: Custom BPF root path, or empty to use defaults\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nCheckOrMountFS(logger, \"\")  // Use default paths\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\n### Action Type\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate   Action = iota  // Value inserted or updated\n    MapDelete              // Value deleted\n    MapDeleteAll           // All values deleted\n)\n\nfunc (a Action) String() string  // \"update\", \"delete\", or \"delete-all\"\n```\n\n### Event Type\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp     time.Time\n    // Private fields: action, cacheEntry\n}\n\n// Public accessor methods:\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string      // String representation of action\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string          // String representation of key\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string        // String representation of value\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error     // Error if the operation failed\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction  // Sync state\n```\n\n### WithCache\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Enables value caching for the map.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Maintains an in-memory cache of all entries inserted from user-space\n- Tracks the desired action (`OK`, `Insert`, `Delete`) for each entry\n- Tracks errors for entries that failed to sync\n- Enables automatic error recovery via the error resolver\n- Returns `m` for method chaining\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0).WithCache()\n```\n\n### WithEvents\n\n```go\ntype BPFEventBufferConfig struct {\n    Enabled bool\n    MaxSize int\n    TTL     time.Duration\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Enables an event buffer that records all map operations.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Stores all `MapUpdate`, `MapDelete`, and `MapDeleteAll` events in a ring buffer\n- Allows events to be dumped and subscribed to via `DumpAndSubscribe()`\n- If TTL is non-zero, old events are periodically removed via a GC controller\n- Approximate memory usage: 100MB per million capacity in `MaxSize`\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `Enabled`: Whether to enable the event buffer\n- `MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to buffer\n- `TTL`: Event time-to-live (0 means events never expire)\n\n**Returns**: `m` for method chaining.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 10000,\n        TTL:     5 * time.Minute,\n    })\n```\n\n### DumpAndSubscribe\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Dumps existing events and optionally subscribes to new events.\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `ctx`: Context for the subscription (used to cancel following)\n- `callback`: Called for each existing event and new events (if `follow` is true)\n- `follow`: If true, continues to invoke callback for new events; if false, only dumps existing events\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Acquires a read lock\n- Iterates over the event buffer and invokes the callback for each valid (non-expired) event\n- If `follow` is true, registers the callback as an observer for new events\n- The subscription is tied to the context's lifetime\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"[%s] %s: %s -> %s (error: %v)\\n\",\n        e.GetAction(),\n        e.GetKey(),\n        e.GetValue(),\n        e.GetLastError(),\n    )\n}, true)  // true to follow new events\n\n// Later, when you want to stop receiving events:\ncancel()\n```\n\n### IsEventsEnabled\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns whether the event buffer is enabled.\n\n**Returns**: True if events are being buffered, false otherwise.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants for datapath runtime configuration\n    Constants any\n\n    // Maps to rename during loading\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Existing Map instances to reuse (wrapped ebpf.Map references)\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to write configuration dump\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (\n    *ebpf.Collection,\n    func() error,  // commit function\n    error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Loads an eBPF collection (programs and maps) into the kernel.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Validates that all programs have specified types (checks for `UnspecifiedProgram`)\n- Renames maps according to `opts.MapRenames`\n- Applies constants from `opts.Constants` to the spec\n- Computes reachability and removes unused programs and maps\n- Resolves tail calls and populates the tail call map\n- Handles map replacements for incompatible pinned maps\n- Returns a function that must be called after programs are attached to commit pending map pins\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `logger`: Logger for diagnostic messages\n- `spec`: The eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Configuration options (can be nil for defaults)\n\n**Returns**:\n- An `ebpf.Collection` with loaded programs and maps\n- A `commit` function that finalizes map pinning (must be called after attaching programs)\n- An error if loading fails\n\n**Example**:\n```go\ncoll, commit, err := LoadCollection(logger, spec, &CollectionOptions{\n    Constants: &myConfig,\n    MapRenames: []map[string]string{\n        {\"old_name\": \"new_name\"},\n    },\n})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs...\nattachProgram(coll.Programs[\"my_prog\"])\n\n// Finalize map pins\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (\n    func() error,  // commit function\n    error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Loads a collection and assigns the results to struct fields.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Analyzes the target struct to determine which objects to keep\n- Calls `LoadCollection()` with auto-detected keep set\n- Assigns programs and maps from the collection to matching fields in the target struct\n- Returns the commit function for finalizing map pins\n- On verifier errors, prints the verifier log to stderr\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `logger`: Logger for diagnostic messages\n- `to`: A pointer to a struct with fields for programs and maps\n- `spec`: The eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Configuration options (can be nil for defaults)\n\n**Returns**:\n- A `commit` function (must be called after attaching programs)\n- An error if loading or assignment fails\n\n**Example**:\n```go\ntype MyPrograms struct {\n    KProbe *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"my_kprobe\"`\n    MyMap  *ebpf.Map     `ebpf:\"my_map\"`\n}\n\nvar progs MyPrograms\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, &progs, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs...\nlink, err := link.Kprobe(\"some_func\", progs.KProbe)\n\n// Finalize\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Advanced Features\n\n### Map with Cache Tracking\n\nWhen `WithCache()` is enabled:\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0).WithCache()\n```\n\nEach entry has a `DesiredAction` state:\n- **OK**: Entry is in sync between user-space and kernel\n- **Insert**: Entry update to kernel failed; will be retried automatically\n- **Delete**: Entry deletion from kernel failed; will be retried automatically\n\nThe error resolver runs periodically and attempts to resolve entries in `Insert` or `Delete` states.\n\n### WithPressureMetric\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Enables tracking of map capacity pressure.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Reports a metric when the map usage exceeds the threshold\n- Pressure is calculated as `(cache_size) / (max_entries)`\n- Only reported when enabled in metrics configuration\n\n### WithGroupName\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Sets the metric group name for this map.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Groups metrics for multiple maps of the same type\n- Useful for aggregating metrics across multiple map instances\n\n### GetModel\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) GetModel() *models.BPFMap\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns an API representation of the map state (for REST API responses).\n\n**Returns**: A `models.BPFMap` containing the map's path and cache entries.\n\n### BatchCount\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the number of elements in the map using a batch lookup.\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Only works for Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps\n- Uses batched lookups for efficiency\n- Automatically handles buffer sizing and retries on `ENOSPC`\n\n**Returns**: The element count, or an error if unsupported map type or operation fails.\n\n### NextKey\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Gets the next key after the given key (for iteration).\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Passes through to the underlying `ebpf.Map.NextKey()`\n- Acquires a read lock for thread-safe access\n- Useful for manual iteration when batched iteration is not available\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `key`: The current key (nil to get the first key)\n- `nextKeyOut`: Pointer to write the next key to\n\n**Returns**: An error, including `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` when iteration is complete.\n\n### Type\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Returns the map type (Hash, Array, etc.).\n\n**Returns**: The `ebpf.MapType` from the spec if the map isn't open, or from the kernel if it is.\n\n### KeySize, ValueSize, MaxEntries, Flags\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32\n```\n\n**Purpose**: Return the map's configuration parameters.\n\n**Returns**: The respective values from the map spec or kernel map.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Types\n\n- `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`: Key was not found in the map\n- `ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible`: Existing map is incompatible with spec\n- `unix.ENOSPC`: No space in batch lookup buffer (handled automatically by BatchIterator)\n- `ErrMapNotOpened`: Map is not open (for reconciler operations)\n- `ErrMaxLookup`: Iteration limit exceeded during reliable dump\n\n### Error Recovery\n\nMaps with `WithCache()` enabled have automatic error recovery:\n\n1. When an operation fails, the cache entry is marked with `DesiredAction = Insert` or `Delete`\n2. An error resolver controller is scheduled\n3. The resolver periodically attempts to sync failed entries\n4. Once successful, the `DesiredAction` is set to `OK`\n\n---\n\n## EndpointKey Example\n\n```go\n// EndpointKey represents the key for the endpoints map\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 `align:\"$union0\"`  // IPv6 or IPv4 (lowest 4 bytes)\n    Family    uint8      `align:\"family\"`   // EndpointKeyIPv4 or EndpointKeyIPv6\n    Key       uint8      `align:\"key\"`\n    ClusterID uint16     `align:\"cluster_id\"`\n}\n\nconst (\n    EndpointKeyIPv4 uint8 = 1\n    EndpointKeyIPv6 uint8 = 2\n)\n\n// NewEndpointKey creates a key from an IP address\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    result := EndpointKey{}\n    if addr.Is4() {\n        result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv4\n    } else if addr.Is6() {\n        result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv6\n    }\n    copy(result.IP[:], addr.AsSlice())\n    result.ClusterID = clusterID\n    return result\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    addr := k.ToAddr()\n    if addr.IsValid() {\n        return fmt.Sprintf(\"%s:%d\", addr, k.Key)\n    }\n    return \"nil\"\n}\n\n// Usage\nkey := NewEndpointKey(netip.MustParseAddr(\"10.0.0.1\"), 0)\nvalue, err := endpointMap.Lookup(&key)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Always pair Open/OpenOrCreate with Close**: Use defer to ensure cleanup.\n\n2. **Use DeleteLocked only in callbacks**: Always use `DeleteLocked` when deleting entries within `DumpWithCallback` or similar contexts where the lock is already held.\n\n3. **Enable caching for error recovery**: Use `WithCache()` when you need automatic retry on failures.\n\n4. **Use BatchIterator for large maps**: More efficient than `DumpWithCallback` for maps with many entries.\n\n5. **Use DumpReliablyWithCallback for concurrent modifications**: When the map might be modified while iterating, use reliable dump.\n\n6. **Check map existence with DumpIfExists**: When the map might not exist yet, use `DumpIfExists` or `DumpWithCallbackIfExists` to avoid errors.\n\n7. **Enable events for auditing**: Use `WithEvents()` when you need to track all map modifications for auditing or debugging.\n\n8. **Handle ErrMaxLookup**: In `DumpReliablyWithCallback`, be prepared to handle `ErrMaxLookup` if the map is continuously updated.\n\n---\n\n## Thread Safety\n\nAll Map operations are thread-safe:\n\n- `Lookup()` acquires a read lock\n- `Update()` and `Delete()` acquire a write lock\n- `Open()` and `Close()` serialize with a write lock\n- `DumpWithCallback()` acquires a read lock\n- Iterator-based operations respect the lock hierarchy\n\nExternal synchronization is not required for concurrent access, but be aware that:\n\n- `DeleteLocked()` must only be called when you hold the write lock (i.e., from within a callback)\n- Pinned maps can be accessed from multiple processes\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\nFor more details on eBPF maps and the cilium/ebpf library, consult:\n\n- The `cilium/ebpf` package documentation: https://github.com/cilium/ebpf\n- Linux kernel eBPF documentation\n- Cilium project documentation\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":802,"cache_read_input_tokens":65983,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":802},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"145b40f5-5bd6-450e-b9e2-2b500f8a89a9","uuid":"cc067f0c-d9cd-4d53-9479-54674cd71448"}
